  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'

<span id="freeTextContainer12821857388662226438">Tracy Crosswhite has spent twenty years questioning the facts surrounding her sister Sarah’s disappearance and the murder trial that followed. She doesn’t believe that Edmund House — a convicted rapist and the man condemned for Sarah’s murder — is the guilty party. Motivated by the opportunity to obtain real justice, Tracy became a homicide detective with the Seattle PD an</span>
  <span id="freeText12821857388662226438" style="display:none">Tracy Crosswhite has spent twenty years questioning the facts surrounding her sister Sarah’s disappearance and the murder trial that followed. She doesn’t believe that Edmund House — a convicted rapist and the man condemned for Sarah’s murder — is the guilty party. Motivated by the opportunity to obtain real justice, Tracy became a homicide detective with the Seattle PD and dedicated her life to tracking down killers.<br /><br />When Sarah’s remains are finally discovered near their hometown in the northern Cascade mountains of Washington State, Tracy is determined to get the answers she’s been seeking. As she searches for the real killer, she unearths dark, long-kept secrets that will forever change her relationship to her past — and open the door to deadly danger.</span>

<div id="review_2452776455" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2452776455" />
    <a title="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24156068-christina---recipe-a-read"><img alt="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580849831p2/24156068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2452776455?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" href="/user/show/24156068-christina---recipe-a-read">Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24156068-christina---recipe-a-read?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2452776455" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer278572850169158863"><b>I can not</b> <br/><i>I can not</i><br/><b>I can not give</b><br/><i>I can not give</i><br/><b>I can not give this book the full 5 stars</b><br/><i>I can not give this book the full 5 stars but I can give it 3.5 and round her up to</i> <b>4 stars</b><i>!!!</i><br/><br/>Most mystery/thriller novels are fairly formulaic but while I <i>know</i> this, I generally don't <i>feel</i> it while I'm reading. I've spent some time in *deep meditation* culling through all the reasons this could be and after communing with some book gods and spirit animals I've come up with my top three:<br/><br/>1) I am a maverick. I </span>
  <span id="freeText278572850169158863" style="display:none"><b>I can not</b> <br /><i>I can not</i><br /><b>I can not give</b><br /><i>I can not give</i><br /><b>I can not give this book the full 5 stars</b><br /><i>I can not give this book the full 5 stars but I can give it 3.5 and round her up to</i> <b>4 stars</b><i>!!!</i><br /><br />Most mystery/thriller novels are fairly formulaic but while I <i>know</i> this, I generally don't <i>feel</i> it while I'm reading. I've spent some time in *deep meditation* culling through all the reasons this could be and after communing with some book gods and spirit animals I've come up with my top three:<br /><br />1) I am a maverick. I cannot be held down by the confines of typicality. <br />2) I have an incredible ability to connect with all stories.<br /><br /><i>Jury is still out but I'll put all my money on what's behind door number three.</i><br /><br />3) I'm a pure and simple GARBAGE DETECTIVE and therefore am surprised constantly. <br /><br />This was such a juxtaposition of formulaic and fresh for me it's hard to put into words. As I mentioned, I've never really felt the true formula of mystery novels until <i>My Sister's Grave</i>. At times I was <b>painfully</b> aware of the equation and it made it impossible to ignore and engross myself. However, despite this I found myself surprised and delighted by the twists and turns of this story. <br /><br />Tracy Crosswhite lost her sister Sarah 20 years ago. Since her disappearance her body has never been found and a man named Edmund House rots in jail - all the while Tracy feels like she never got the full story and was ignored when she presented key findings that contradicted the evidence. The story pretty much starts with the uncovering of remains that turn out to be Sarah's and thus it reopens old wounds for the town and for Tracy, who lost everything the day she lost her sister. <br /><br />This is told in third person narrative and is segmented into two parts. Part one, starting with the finding of Sarah's remains and with ever increasing flashbacks to Tracy and Sarah's childhood and her subsequent disappearance. Part two, I'll leave for future readers to figure out on their own so I don't spoil anything but know that it packs a punch! <br /><br />The characters here were all, for the most part (aside from the "bad guys") really likable and believable. There really isn't any wasted time on superfluous red herrings but I still felt myself questioning everything as the story was laid out. There is a lot of subtlety here and it was a nice break from the 'in your face-ness' that happens a lot in this genre. <br /><br />I ultimately rounded up instead of down for this one because I've been reading <b>a lot</b> of thrillers recently and while they're all emotional to some degree I've not been brought to tears by any of them. This surprised me with the depth of the characters, especially the relationship between Tracy and Sarah. There were multiple points here that had my eyes misting and texting my own sister how much I love her. <br /><br />This was a smartly written, slow simmering mystery that I enjoyed quite a bit. It was character driven and the development here was top notch. It was enjoyable and well paced and I think I'll certainly be picking up the second novel in this series down the line!</span>
  <a data-text-id="278572850169158863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2317784242" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2317784242" />
    <a title="James Thane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3483907-james-thane"><img alt="James Thane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442513566p2/3483907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2317784242?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Thane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Thane" href="/user/show/3483907-james-thane">James Thane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3483907-james-thane?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2317784242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13181629472393458097"><i>My Sister's Grave</i> introduces Seattle homicide detective Tracy Crosswhite. Twenty years earlier, her younger sister, Sarah, who was then eighteen, disappeared after the two had participated in a shooting competition. As Tracy went off to dinner with her boyfriend, Sarah left to drive home in the rain and was never seen again. <br/><br/>The two sisters had been best of friends and Tracy has never forgiven herself for allowing Sarah to drive home alone. Twenty years later, the pain is still sharp and ultimat</span>
  <span id="freeText13181629472393458097" style="display:none"><i>My Sister's Grave</i> introduces Seattle homicide detective Tracy Crosswhite. Twenty years earlier, her younger sister, Sarah, who was then eighteen, disappeared after the two had participated in a shooting competition. As Tracy went off to dinner with her boyfriend, Sarah left to drive home in the rain and was never seen again. <br /><br />The two sisters had been best of friends and Tracy has never forgiven herself for allowing Sarah to drive home alone. Twenty years later, the pain is still sharp and ultimately led Tracy to give up her career as a teacher to become a homicide detective. <br /><br />A previously convicted rapist named Edmund House was arrested and convicted of Sarah's murder, largely on the basis of circumstantial evidence and on the testimony of the local sheriff who claimed that House had confessed to killing Sarah, even though there was no tape recording or witness to back up the sheriff's claim. Tracy has never been totally convinced of House's guilt and has continued digging into the case in an effort to satisfy herself of the fact that justice either was or was not done.<br /><br />As the book opens, Sarah's remains are finally found by two hunters in a heavily wooded area that had previously been covered by a lake. The discovery of the body raises even more questions about the case against Edmund House and makes Tracy even more determined to make sure that the person who killed her sister pays the price. Her efforts will antagonize a good number of people in the small town where she grew up and where the crime occurred. They will also place Tracy herself in a considerable amount of jeopardy.<br /><br />This is a very compelling story that combines the best elements of a legal thriller with that of a gripping police procedural. Tracy Crosswhite makes a very engaging protagonist and the story moves at such a fast clip that it's almost impossible to put the book down once it gets rolling. All in all, a very good introduction to this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13181629472393458097" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1049528592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9623606140224722635">It's been a good year for this crime fiction fanatic. I have read some really good books in this genre and this is no exception. My Sister's Grave has a really interesting plot and grabbed me from the word go, I read up to the 80% mark in one sitting, then sadly had to sleep, but finished it when I woke up. Not one minute of boredom whilst reading this. <br/><br/><i>Tracy Crosswhite has spent twenty years questioning the facts surrounding her sister Sarah’s disappearance and the murder trial that followed. S</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9623606140224722635" style="display:none">It's been a good year for this crime fiction fanatic. I have read some really good books in this genre and this is no exception. My Sister's Grave has a really interesting plot and grabbed me from the word go, I read up to the 80% mark in one sitting, then sadly had to sleep, but finished it when I woke up. Not one minute of boredom whilst reading this. <br /><br /><i>Tracy Crosswhite has spent twenty years questioning the facts surrounding her sister Sarah’s disappearance and the murder trial that followed. She doesn’t believe that Edmund House—a convicted rapist and the man condemned for Sarah’s murder—is the guilty party. Motivated by the opportunity to obtain real justice, Tracy became a homicide detective with the Seattle PD and dedicated her life to tracking down killers.<br /><br />When Sarah’s remains are finally discovered near their hometown in the northern Cascade mountains of Washington State, Tracy is determined to get the answers she’s been seeking. As she searches for the real killer, she unearths dark, long-kept secrets that will forever change her relationship to her past—and open the door to deadly danger.</i><br /><br /><b>You know the term "let sleeping dogs lie?" - yes, well Tracy should have done this.</b> But despite warnings to leave the case alone, Tracy won't rest until she sees the investigation into her sister's death reopened. She doesn't believe the evidence presented and with the help of her friend/lover/blast from the past lawyer, the can of worms is indeed opened up again. <br /><br /><b>It's got one of those plots where you really can see some things coming, but they are planted to be that obvious because even the reveals are interesting and contain a few things you would not expect. I liked that. I liked that I was tipped slightly off-kilter a few times. The build up to the finish of this book is gradual, with tension mounting and events rolling out until nothing can stop where it is heading. And it ain't pretty.</b> <br /><br />The characters are really well written, I loved Tracy's loyalty and love for her dead sister, admired her for not giving up on seeking answers. I want her to be my sister, I know at least if I got murdered, my sister would not rest until the truth was out there. I digress slightly into fantasising about not being an only child anymore...<br /><br />It's just a really good book, it's highly entertaining and keeps you alert and wanting more, you will want to power through pages to get to the final outcome. I freaking loved the last few chapters, I was out of my seat and cheering for some characters and yelling at others. <br /><br /><b>One of my memorable crime fiction reads of 2014. Awesome sauce.<br /><br />I am not afraid of the dark,<br />I am not afraid of the dark,<br />I am not afraid.</b><br /><br />Check out more of my reviews, book giveaways, book talk and more at:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/BookloverCatlady">https://www.facebook.com/BookloverCat...</a><br /><br /><i>A copy of this book was given to my thanks to the publisher via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review, many thanks.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9623606140224722635" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1655961910" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1655961910" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9472704-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336837712p2/9472704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1655961910?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/9472704-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=robert-dugoni">robert-dugoni</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=mystery-thrillers">mystery-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1655961910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17735774613569159719">Well now.....<br/><br/>"You're not a crazy person, Tracy. Obsessed, maybe."<br/><br/>Tracy Crosswhite still looks over her shoulder in the direction of her sister's murder twenty years ago. You never get over the death of a loved one and you can never quite cross the bridge. That bridge is paved with the stones of so many unanswered questions and no physical remains.<br/><br/>Tracy and her sister, Sarah, were inseparable until the night of her disappearance. Gone. Vanished. Out of sight. But the tragedy lingers and takes its</span>
  <span id="freeText17735774613569159719" style="display:none">Well now.....<br /><br />"You're not a crazy person, Tracy. Obsessed, maybe."<br /><br />Tracy Crosswhite still looks over her shoulder in the direction of her sister's murder twenty years ago. You never get over the death of a loved one and you can never quite cross the bridge. That bridge is paved with the stones of so many unanswered questions and no physical remains.<br /><br />Tracy and her sister, Sarah, were inseparable until the night of her disappearance. Gone. Vanished. Out of sight. But the tragedy lingers and takes its toll. The family dynamics change forever. Tracy re-invents herself from chemistry teacher to a Seattle detective leaving the likes of her small town of Cedar Grove in the rearview mirror.<br /><br />Her experiential background leaves an unsettled feeling about how the murder case was handled by the local police. Although Edmund House was convicted of the crime, Tracy is not sure that justice prevailed. She is convinced that there is more to what meets the eye here. The memory of it all is suffocating her mind, heart, and soul. And the only road to peace is to tread down its pathway once again.<br /><br />I like my mystery/thrillers smart and aboveboard with no eyerolling adventures that take you in an illogical free-fall off a deluded cliff. You all know what I'm talking about.<br /><br />Robert Dugoni creates his lead character as an intelligent, no nonsense, analytically reasoning female. Just the way I like it. <br /><br />And here's the bonus. Dugoni knows his way around a courtroom. The dialogue reflects just that. He reaches into corners untapped and left behind in the shadows. His characters are well-developed and the coffee cup doesn't overflow with unnecessary bogus information. There is plenty of deep-seeded emotion here without leaving sticky footprints behind. Just the facts, mam, just the facts.<br /><br />I'm sold on this series and am looking forward to the rest of them in this Dugoni Dynasty. Simply good writing and a solid storyline. You've got my attention, Dugoni. On to the next!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17735774613569159719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1072198927" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1072198927" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26175098-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453924875p2/26175098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1072198927?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/26175098-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Christine by: </span>
      Sue 5
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=police-procedural-fbi">police-procedural-fbi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=1st-of-series">1st-of-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=legal-thriller">legal-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1072198927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2370367548969588722">My interest in this series was peaked by two prequel short stories focused on Detective Tracy Crosswhite’s earlier days. I was really drawn to Tracy while reading The Academy, set during Tracy’s Police Academy days, and knew after reading Third Watch, set during her days as a beat cop in Seattle, that I wanted more of this detective. Though it’s not necessary to read the prequels before launching into the novels, Tracy’s early relationship with her future boss, Johnny Nolasco, is very entertaini</span>
  <span id="freeText2370367548969588722" style="display:none">My interest in this series was peaked by two prequel short stories focused on Detective Tracy Crosswhite’s earlier days. I was really drawn to Tracy while reading The Academy, set during Tracy’s Police Academy days, and knew after reading Third Watch, set during her days as a beat cop in Seattle, that I wanted more of this detective. Though it’s not necessary to read the prequels before launching into the novels, Tracy’s early relationship with her future boss, Johnny Nolasco, is very entertainingly set forth in these shorts, especially The Academy, and both short stories are rated 5 stars by me.<br /><br />As My Sister’s Grave opens, Tracy is 42 years old and a Homicide Detective. Tracy decided to become a law enforcement officer after her sister Sarah disappeared twenty years previously and was never found. Tracy’s ultimate goal is to find out what happened to Sarah and bring justice to her sister. There is an unexpected break in the very cold case, and Tracy is determined to find out once and for all who is responsible for her sister’s disappearance.<br /><br />This is an easy book to fly through. The plot, though pretty straightforward, held my interest throughout, though there are some slower spots during the first third of the story. Once the story gets rolling there is plenty of suspense and some nifty little twists to relish. There is a bit of possible romance, which I never object to. Most importantly, I was fooled in the end, always a plus. There is more courtroom action than I expected, but I was surprised to find that I really enjoyed it. I must read more legal thrillers as I think I’ve been missing out. <br /> <br />I loved, loved, loved Tracy’s character and especially delighted in how she interacts with Johnny Nolasco. Tracy is actually nice! She has no issues relating to others, a positive change from many of the protagonists we see in crime fiction these days. Don’t misunderstand; she is not a wimp and definitely does not let anyone steamroll her. I am stoked to read more Tracy Crosswhite.<br /><br />My Sister’s Grave is a good solid start to the series. From what I’ve heard from others, the novels only get better from here. I plan to be on board for the full run.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2370367548969588722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7911510358641153041">Tracy Crosswhite loses her sister, Sarah, who disappears without a trace, when they were young. Tracy uses this watershed of an event to enroll as a homicide detective. When someone is caught as the killer of her sister, Tracy doesn't believe he did it, for reasons of her own.<br/><br/>Sarah's body is discovered and that sets the ball rolling for the appeasement and peace of mind for Tracy, and closure too. Recently I've been reading lots of first books in their series where the victim is someone very clo</span>
  <span id="freeText7911510358641153041" style="display:none">Tracy Crosswhite loses her sister, Sarah, who disappears without a trace, when they were young. Tracy uses this watershed of an event to enroll as a homicide detective. When someone is caught as the killer of her sister, Tracy doesn't believe he did it, for reasons of her own.<br /><br />Sarah's body is discovered and that sets the ball rolling for the appeasement and peace of mind for Tracy, and closure too. Recently I've been reading lots of first books in their series where the victim is someone very close to the main character. These type of books are heavily attractive as a standalone effort.<br /><br />I liked this book. It grew on me. I liked Tracy's near and dear people. The courtroom scenes are well enacted. I've got no complaints, really. The author is spot on in his details of the cases Tracy handles. Of course, the murderer is found, Of course, Tracy gets closure, but the ride is well worth the read.</span>

<div id="review_1099979826" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1099979826" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277905205p2/1166663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1099979826?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166663-carol?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166663-carol?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166663-carol?shelf=cold-case">cold-case</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166663-carol?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1099979826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11107736599536337894"><b>The Hook</b> - <u>My Sister’s Grave</u> has been on my TBR list for a long time. The price was right and so was my mood. <br/><br/><b>The Line</b> - The epigraph <br/><br/><i>”Better that ten guilty persons escape than that one innocent suffer.<br/> --SIR WILLIAM BLACKSTONE, Commentaries on the Laws of England”</i><br/><br/><b>The Sinker</b> - It’s twenty years, twenty long years to wonder where the body of your sister has been buried. You were the big sister, you were responsible for her and yet you put your own happiness ahead of that and let her drive home a</span>
  <span id="freeText11107736599536337894" style="display:none"><b>The Hook</b> - <u>My Sister’s Grave</u> has been on my TBR list for a long time. The price was right and so was my mood. <br /><br /><b>The Line</b> - The epigraph <br /><br /><i>”Better that ten guilty persons escape than that one innocent suffer.<br /> --SIR WILLIAM BLACKSTONE, Commentaries on the Laws of England”</i><br /><br /><b>The Sinker</b> - It’s twenty years, twenty long years to wonder where the body of your sister has been buried. You were the big sister, you were responsible for her and yet you put your own happiness ahead of that and let her drive home alone during a bitter, brutal winter storm. You warned her to stick to the highway and avoid the dark, isolated country road to your home. When your truck is found on that road, locked and empty, at first you think she’s home. But no, she’s gone and the guilt is yours.<br /><br />The character outlined above is Tracy Crosswhite, now a Seattle homicide detective. While working a case she receives notice that two hunters have found the remains of a body in the hills above her hometown, Cedar Grove. Is this the body of her long missing sister Sarah? <br /><br />Robert Dugoni drew me in like a spider to his web. In flashbacks we come to know the Crosswhite family, particularly the bond between the sisters. Cedar Grove, north of Seattle, is a small town with all that comes with that. People know people, the friendships go back years and everyone takes care of their own. Dugoni is a very descriptive in this chilly cold case mystery both in character development and setting. Winter and all its fury come to life under his pen and he fleshes out the characters so I feel an emotional connection. Some may consider the pacing slow for a mystery/thriller. I thought it was just right, brooding at times, thoughtful, building momentum and tension as I accelerated to its finish. <br /><br />Dugoni has many books under his belt. <u>My Sister’s Grave</u> was intended as a standalone but fans wanted more and I can see why. There are now three Tracy Crosswhite police procedurals and a 0.5 that I’m assuming is a prequel. Tracy Crosswhite is a strong and determined woman with a potential for complexity that I’d like to explore. I’ve already grabbed the second in the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11107736599536337894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1275147120" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1275147120" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1275147120?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=mystery-shelf">mystery-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1275147120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11857371430280740682">My Sister’s Grave by Robert Dugoni is a 2014 Thomas & Mercer publication<br/><br/>This book has been sitting in my TBR pile for a long time, but finally made it to the top of the heap. This is a pleasure read for me and I am so glad I finally got to enjoy it. <br/><br/>This is a unique thriller that kept me guessing all the way to the horrifying conclusion that had me on the edge of my seat and in complete shock. <br/><br/>Twenty years ago, Tracy Crosswhite’s world caved in when her younger sister disappeared. Although there</span>
  <span id="freeText11857371430280740682" style="display:none">My Sister’s Grave by Robert Dugoni is a 2014 Thomas &amp; Mercer publication<br /><br />This book has been sitting in my TBR pile for a long time, but finally made it to the top of the heap. This is a pleasure read for me and I am so glad I finally got to enjoy it. <br /><br />This is a unique thriller that kept me guessing all the way to the horrifying conclusion that had me on the edge of my seat and in complete shock. <br /><br />Twenty years ago, Tracy Crosswhite’s world caved in when her younger sister disappeared. Although there was a conviction in the case, her sister’s body was never found… until now. <br /><br />In the years since her sister disappeared, Tracy quits her teaching job, moved to Seattle, and became a homicide detective, while working on her sister’s case whenever possible. Tracy never bought into the theory that the man accused of killing her sister was guilty. Now that Sarah’s body has been found, Tracy hires her childhood friend, Dan, to help her prove the wrong man was convicted. But, the local sheriff pulls out all the stops to make sure a new trial never takes place. Was there a conspiracy? Who really killed Sarah and how will Tracy manage to prove it? <br /><br />It took only a couple of chapters to hook me into this story. Tracy is a person riddled with guilt over what happened to her sister, but is tenacious to the point of obsession in her determination to see justice done. I was enthralled by the small town secrets, manipulations, and the legal wrangling which was top notch, and something I really miss in crime novels these days. The twists are subtle and I fell headlong into the clever trap set for me. I was a little miffed, I suppose, by being fooled so handily, but also by the faulty reasoning of some people. I can’t say more than that, but it was a sticky situation and perhaps a moral dilemma that could provoke some heated debate. I know what side of the fence, I would come down on because the truth does have a way of coming to light no matter how deeply it’s buried. <br /><br /><br />I think this book dabbled in many sub-genres of crime fiction adding a dab of legal thriller, a smidgen of psychological thriller, a slice of whodunit mystery and a sprinkle of suspense, blending them all together to create a top notch thriller. The dialogue is smart and believable, and I appreciated the portrayal of a lead female character as being both smart and sensitive, and thankfully level headed and grounded. I’m not sure how she felt about the whole sordid mess once all was said and done, and I wonder if she feels the same way I do, but I do think she will be able to live her life fully now that she knows the whole truth about Sarah and what really happened to her. <br /><br />I have continued to ruminate over this story and think about how everything played out which means it made an impression on me and has stuck with me for a while, and that’s always a good sign the author has done a good job in keeping me engaged, even after the book is finished. <br /><br />Overall, this is an emotional story, a very smart thriller, through provoking and very original. I will most definitely be back for more Robert Dugoni novels!! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11857371430280740682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1150422541741649132"><br/>I wish to thank Amazon Publishing, Thomas & Mercer and NetGalley for an ARC in exchange for an honest review.<br/><br/>"MY SISTER’S GRAVE" by Robert Dugoni is a great legal thriller mixed with a classic police procedural. It is a gripping emotional and strong character-driven suspense legal thriller, of one woman’s mission to find her sister’s real killer.<br/><br/>This book was very entertaining.   <span id="freeText1150422541741649132" style="display:none"><br />I wish to thank Amazon Publishing, Thomas &amp; Mercer and NetGalley for an ARC in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />"MY SISTER’S GRAVE" by Robert Dugoni is a great legal thriller mixed with a classic police procedural. It is a gripping emotional and strong character-driven suspense legal thriller, of one woman’s mission to find her sister’s real killer.<br /><br />This book was very entertaining. The short chapter format briskly moves the story along. The characters are well-written, engaging, and the plot was believable. <br /><br />Detective Tracy Crosswhite,42 years old, from the Seattle homicide, lost her younger sister Sarah, over twenty years ago, when she disappeared and feels somewhat responsible. The sisters had been involved in the sport of shooting, and after a championship, Sarah, was kidnapped and murdered, her body was never found. A local man on parole for rape, was arrested and convicted of the crime. Tracy never believed he was the real killer. <br /><br />When a young woman’s remains are discovered, in a shallow grave,Tracy returns to her mountain hometown of Cedar Grove, WA. <br /><br />Tracy is now determined to solve the mystery and find the real killer. With the help of Don O’Leary, a childhood friend and now a lawyer, agrees to help her.<br /><br /><br />But what really happened that one night so long ago?<br /><br />This novel will appeal to fans of legal crime thrillers, courtroom dramas, investigations, and police procedures with well-developed characters, in a small town setting...with a twisted ending.<br /> <br />I definitely enjoyed reading this novel, and had it not been for Christmas and the holidays , I would have devoured it faster.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1616130571" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1616130571" />
    <a title="Sheila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6810645-sheila"><img alt="Sheila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460570342p2/6810645.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1616130571?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sheila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sheila" href="/user/show/6810645-sheila">Sheila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6810645-sheila?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6810645-sheila?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1616130571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer933761271425061668">I'm going to be a curmudgeon for a moment. <br/><br/>It takes two things to make a great book (OK, that's oversimplified, but bear with me a sec): Being able to tell a good story, and being able to write well. This book has a pretty good grasp on the first part, but utterly fails on the second.<br/><br/>The book's plot is fine, if unoriginal--it's nothing we haven't seen before (a cop with a murdered sibling/spouse/child is practically a requirement for a suspense novel), but it makes sense and has a good grasp of </span>
  <span id="freeText933761271425061668" style="display:none">I'm going to be a curmudgeon for a moment. <br /><br />It takes two things to make a great book (OK, that's oversimplified, but bear with me a sec): Being able to tell a good story, and being able to write well. This book has a pretty good grasp on the first part, but utterly fails on the second.<br /><br />The book's plot is fine, if unoriginal--it's nothing we haven't seen before (a cop with a murdered sibling/spouse/child is practically a requirement for a suspense novel), but it makes sense and has a good grasp of how to move characters around, push the story forward, and resolve things adequately. (That's not easy to do, it's worth noting.)<br /><br />However, the writing is atrocious. I'm a copy editor, but when I read for fun, I like to shut off that part of my brain and leave it at work. When a book's grammar is so bad it pulls me out of the story and makes me get out my mental red pen, I get cranky! This book (like all Amazon's imprints--at least that I've read) needs a good proofreading: it lacks important commas, uses the wrong word repeatedly (compliment instead of complement; board instead of bored), and misplaces modifiers all over the place. Dialogue is clunky too. But even fixing those things wouldn't make this good writing. The book's worst failing is its lack of sentence variety. Almost every sentence starts with subject, verb, over and over again. (There were 10 sentences in a row that started this way. "He went..." "Tracy noticed..." "They took..." etc.) This is dull and repetitive. Characters could use some work too--I'm not sure any of them rose above stereotypes (but, this seems to be another standard of the genre).<br /><br />I'm giving this 2 stars ("it was okay") instead of 1 because, like I said, the story held together. I read to the end to find out "who dun it." There was even a court scene in the middle which I thought was nicely done, and I appreciate that the author didn't give us the gory details of what happened to the victim. But I doubt I'll read any more of this author's work unless his writing significantly improves.<br /><br />I received this review copy from the publisher on NetGalley. Thanks for the opportunity to read and review; I appreciate it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="933761271425061668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1358519050" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1358519050" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1358519050?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=mystery-thriller-etc">mystery-thriller-etc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=kindle-unlimited">kindle-unlimited</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1358519050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12241945232141917469">MY BLOG: <a href='http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2015/12/my-sisters-grave-by-robert-dugoni.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451166706i/17513177.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I thought the book was good! There are a lot of twists and turns for sure! And I didn't even pay attention that this is the first book so I'm guessing this is a series! Yay! I like Tracy Crosswhite's character. <br/><br/>Tracy is a detective, she decided this when her sister Sarah disappeared 20 years ago and there was never any closure for Tracy. The town of Cedar Grove put a man named Edmund House away for the crime, but something seemed off to Tracy...none of the e</span>
  <span id="freeText12241945232141917469" style="display:none">MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2015/12/my-sisters-grave-by-robert-dugoni.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451166706i/17513177.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I thought the book was good! There are a lot of twists and turns for sure! And I didn't even pay attention that this is the first book so I'm guessing this is a series! Yay! I like Tracy Crosswhite's character. <br><br>Tracy is a detective, she decided this when her sister Sarah disappeared 20 years ago and there was never any closure for Tracy. The town of Cedar Grove put a man named Edmund House away for the crime, but something seemed off to Tracy...none of the evidence seemed right, but no one would listen to her. The town, including her father, said it was Edmund because he was in jail for a short 6 years for beating and raping a girl...6 years.. yeah.. <br><br>The book goes back and forth between now and when Tracy and Sarah were last together. You get little clues along the way. Most of it was pretty obvious at one point but then they turn around and throw a twist in there! <br><br>Anyway, so these remains were found by a mans dog while they were out in the woods. These remains were proven to be Tracy's sister Sarah. Tracy immediately goes to Cedar Grove from Seattle to be involved in what is going on. Sarah's remains were found in the woods, but something was weird about the findings....no.. I'm not saying what! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451166706i/17513178.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Tracy and Sarah were friends with Dan and a bunch of kids growing up.. it is a small town. Anyway, Tracy catches up with Dan and he is a lawyer, she asks him to take a look at all of the work she has kept on the case for 20 years. She tells him there are some things that don't add up. Dan decides to take on the case with Tracy because he can see the things she pointed out to him. It's like really... you people just let this go through? <br><br>Oh and Dan has two cool dogs named Sherlock and Rex, they are Rhodesian Ridgeback/Mastiff mixes. Needless to say they are huge and cool. I always have to mention the dogs... moving on... <br><br>Every turn that Tracy and Dan make, they find more secrets and someone starts threatening their lives. I mean you have to have that right? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451166706i/17513179.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It all comes out in the end and it wasn't what I was expecting. Like I said before, some things you know right off the bat, but then the author just twists it around a little bit and your like.. REALLY!?<br><br>All in all, I liked the book a lot and I plan on reading more Tracy Crosswhite books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12241945232141917469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2267085178" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2267085178" />
    <a title="Carolyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn"><img alt="Carolyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546411572p2/19559507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2267085178?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn">Carolyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22744701-my-sister-s-grave">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=murder-mystery">murder-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=legal-drama">legal-drama</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2267085178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8509987935000430144">Tracy Crosswhite has never forgotten the night her younger sister Sarah disappeared twenty years ago. They had been competing in the finals of a shooting competition and afterwards Tracy went out to dinner with her boyfriend Ben leaving eighteen year old Sarah to drive her car home alone. She never made it home and although Tracy's car was found on a lonely backroad, Sarah was never found. A local man, Edmund House, was later convicted of her abduction and murder in with what Tracy has always co</span>
  <span id="freeText8509987935000430144" style="display:none">Tracy Crosswhite has never forgotten the night her younger sister Sarah disappeared twenty years ago. They had been competing in the finals of a shooting competition and afterwards Tracy went out to dinner with her boyfriend Ben leaving eighteen year old Sarah to drive her car home alone. She never made it home and although Tracy's car was found on a lonely backroad, Sarah was never found. A local man, Edmund House, was later convicted of her abduction and murder in with what Tracy has always considered to be circumstantial evidence. Tracy never got over the pain of Sarah's loss and left her teaching job to retrain as a detective and has kept looking for answers to what happened to Sarah that night. Now Sarah's body has been found by some hunters in the mountains with fresh evidence that has Tracy asking for Edmund's conviction to be appealed.<br /><br />This is a great introduction to a new series featuring Tracy Crosswhite. I really like that she is a likeable, normal person without a drinking problem or dysfunctional family life, although quite obsessive in her quest for justice. There are other well drawn characters in Tracy's school friend Dan, now a lawyer, the well loved but flawed Sheriff, Roy Calloway and the convicted killer Edmund House, who is a nasty piece of work, even if Tracy thinks he was framed. The courtroom drama in the scenes where Dan is defending Edmund during his appeal were also well done, as might be expected with the author's legal background and the final dramatic twist made for a very thrilling ending. Overall an exciting mix of legal drama and compelling thriller and a great start to a series. 4.5★</span>
  <a data-text-id="8509987935000430144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1072850009" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12651536638303697253">A smart murder mystery, well-written, and a plot that is not too convoluted. Lead characters are believable. I particularly liked Sheriff Roy Calloway, 'tough as a two dollar steak'. I got a real kick out of George Bovine stopping by the office of Dan O'Leary. Okay, so it's a small town in Washington and not Chicago, but this couldn't have been inadvertent on the author's part. Loved it!<br/><br/>This was a Kindle-First offering. Enjoyable read. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14214922504743407891">This book is very interesting but explodes in the last third. A sister dies, and the other sister won’t let go for over 20 years. She even becomes a cop to search for the killer. This takes place in the mountains of Washington State and one of the biggest elements of this story is the snow storm. I love how it creeps into the story and finally takes over. You have courtroom drama, a really bad guy, and a woman who can shoot and won’t take no for an answer. You probably won't see the ending comin</span>
  <span id="freeText14214922504743407891" style="display:none">This book is very interesting but explodes in the last third. A sister dies, and the other sister won’t let go for over 20 years. She even becomes a cop to search for the killer. This takes place in the mountains of Washington State and one of the biggest elements of this story is the snow storm. I love how it creeps into the story and finally takes over. You have courtroom drama, a really bad guy, and a woman who can shoot and won’t take no for an answer. You probably won't see the ending coming, even though it's right in front of you. Masterful!<br /><br />This is a really good book from a really good author. Highly recommend!</span>

<div id="review_1392578264" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1392578264" />
    <a title="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede"><img alt="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487436758p2/1379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1392578264?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" href="/user/show/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede">Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1392578264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2137019400759099036"><i>Tracy's sister Sarah disappeared 20 years ago and Edmund House, a convicted rapist is accused and jailed for the murder, despite that they never found the body. But Tracy never believed that Edmund was the real killer. Now Sarah's body is finally discovered and Tracy sets out to find the real killer. But it seems that there are people out there that don't want her to know the truth...</i><br/><br/>I was quickly pulled into this story and read almost 60% of the book in one evening. The story is intense and mov</span>
  <span id="freeText2137019400759099036" style="display:none"><i>Tracy's sister Sarah disappeared 20 years ago and Edmund House, a convicted rapist is accused and jailed for the murder, despite that they never found the body. But Tracy never believed that Edmund was the real killer. Now Sarah's body is finally discovered and Tracy sets out to find the real killer. But it seems that there are people out there that don't want her to know the truth...</i><br /><br />I was quickly pulled into this story and read almost 60% of the book in one evening. The story is intense and moving and I was deeply moved by the story several times. This is a real page-turner. You really want to find out who killed Sarah and who hid her body. There was a moment towards the end when I was a bit confused about why she wanted Edmund released from prison, I mean, he was bad news and releasing him wouldn't bring her sister back. But then I released that with him cleared for the murder could she open the case again and find the real killer. So that made sense that she wanted free him especially since it seemed that he could be framed for the murder.<br /><br />The ending. To be frank. I'm not sure that I really liked it, I saw it as a possibility that it could end something like this. And, it just didn't seem that surprising when the book ended it the way I suspected it would. <br /><br />So this book had a very strong beginning and middle part, a less strong ending. Still good and I will without a doubt read the next book. Especially since I have it waiting for me to be read.<br /><br /><i>Thanks to Thomas &amp; Mercer and NetGalley for providing me with a free copy of this book in exchange for an honest review!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2137019400759099036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1143672193" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1143672193" />
    <a title="Brenda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5240149-brenda"><img alt="Brenda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567952682p2/5240149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1143672193?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenda" href="/user/show/5240149-brenda">Brenda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22744701-my-sister-s-grave">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1143672193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15173538567331050990">This book was a great introduction to Tracy Crosswhite. It shows Tracy and her younger sister, Sarah, during their childhood and teen years. Sarah is about to go to college when she's abducted, and her body was never found. Twenty years later, Tracy is a cop in Seattle, but returns to her childhood home when hunters find a burial site in the woods. It also shows how Tracy is dealing with the guilt and how she's believed all these years that the sheriff, district attorney, and others lied in cour</span>
  <span id="freeText15173538567331050990" style="display:none">This book was a great introduction to Tracy Crosswhite. It shows Tracy and her younger sister, Sarah, during their childhood and teen years. Sarah is about to go to college when she's abducted, and her body was never found. Twenty years later, Tracy is a cop in Seattle, but returns to her childhood home when hunters find a burial site in the woods. It also shows how Tracy is dealing with the guilt and how she's believed all these years that the sheriff, district attorney, and others lied in court.<br /><br />I was immersed in the story and couldn't put it down. The characters felt realistic, with their strengths and weaknesses. I liked Tracy's determination to do what she felt was right, her loyalty to her friends and colleagues, and her strength. I really enjoyed the courtroom scenes and testimony.<br /><br />I read this book as a tribute to Kerry Hunter, a Goodreads friend, who recently passed away. I knew it was a book Kerry loved because she had given it 5 stars and written a strong review. I'm happy to say I agree with her, and I'm looking forward to the next book in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15173538567331050990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2247745042" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2247745042" />
    <a title="Mort" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67602782-mort"><img alt="Mort" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586932919p2/67602782.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2247745042?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mort" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mort" href="/user/show/67602782-mort">Mort</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2247745042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8420354386697310906">Legal thrillers are not really my thing, which is why I can only think of one I've read in the last decade. However, the blurb tickled me and the reviews seemed that it might be worth the risk.<br/><br/>One thing became obvious early on in this novel...Dugoni can write!<br/>He pulled me into this story and kept it interesting throughout. I always cringe with the idea that a crucial piece of evidence will appear right BEFORE the end of the trial, or the lawyer will manage to break a seemingly intelligent person</span>
  <span id="freeText8420354386697310906" style="display:none">Legal thrillers are not really my thing, which is why I can only think of one I've read in the last decade. However, the blurb tickled me and the reviews seemed that it might be worth the risk.<br /><br />One thing became obvious early on in this novel...Dugoni can write!<br />He pulled me into this story and kept it interesting throughout. I always cringe with the idea that a crucial piece of evidence will appear right BEFORE the end of the trial, or the lawyer will manage to break a seemingly intelligent person on the stand, making them confess in court and saving the day JUST when everything seems lost. This writer avoided that. In fact, there was very little of the story that happened inside the courtroom. And, add to that, everything was believable! <br />The best part? He had some wickedly interesting twists in this one and kept the guilty party hidden until very late in the book.<br /><br />The story: Tracy Crosswhite is a Chicago detective, good at her job but haunted by personal demons (and that sounds like a thousand other stories out there, I know, but this gets interesting really fast). Her sister disappeared twenty years ago, her body never discovered, but somebody got caught and was sentenced to life in prison for the murder.<br />She receives notice that a body has been discovered and it might be her sister.<br />The evidence dug up with the body confirms what she has believed for twenty years: They convicted the wrong guy on false circumstantial evidence.<br />Can a detective free a convicted killer to re-open her sister's murder case?<br /><br />If I was nit-picking, I could say that this book could have been a little shorter, but I think it would be unfair to the author. The story was great and everything worked. I loved it.<br />Looking forward to reading the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8420354386697310906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2681371309444030477" style="display:none">While one of the more tame mysteries I've read lately, this is still a solid who-dun-it that has a storyline that was believable. <div id="review_1089518608" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1089518608" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1089518608?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1089518608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1246466658932025554">Dugoni returns after a publication hiatus to introduce the reader to his newest creation, Detective Tracy Crosswhite. In the struggle to come to terms with her sister's kidnapping and suspected murder, Crosswhite cannot help but seek a means of getting much needed answers to end her own speculation. When the body discovered in a wooded area turns out to be that of Sarah Crosswhite, the community is shocked and the drama of the murder resurfaces, even though someone is already serving time for th</span>
  <span id="freeText1246466658932025554" style="display:none">Dugoni returns after a publication hiatus to introduce the reader to his newest creation, Detective Tracy Crosswhite. In the struggle to come to terms with her sister's kidnapping and suspected murder, Crosswhite cannot help but seek a means of getting much needed answers to end her own speculation. When the body discovered in a wooded area turns out to be that of Sarah Crosswhite, the community is shocked and the drama of the murder resurfaces, even though someone is already serving time for the crime. Crosswhite uses all resources at her disposal to push for a reinvestigation into the murder and the trial that sent a man to jail, possibly incarcerating an innocent man. With the help of a childhood friend, Crosswhite leaves no stone unturned to bring justice to her sister and uncover what she feels was shoddy investigation work in the small town of Cedar Grove, Washington. A must-read for Dugoni fans, who pine for a great mystery sprinkled with just the right amount of courtroom drama.<br /><br />Dugoni tells the story in a way that keeps the reader hooked, offering a trail of crumbs to pique interest. He uses regular flashbacks to fill in gaps presented by the modern-day narrative. This technique was, for a time, highly confusing and somewhat overly dramatic. However, it grew on me and helped to tell the story in an effective manner. Dugoni taps into his past experience with courtroom writing and presents a highly controversial mystery sure to keep the reader pushing through, if only to determine who might have been behind the crime in the summer of 1993. The only question that remains with me is how this highly personal novel, whose focus was only minutely on a modern case with a team around her, will act as the foundation of a series, as Dugoni has titled this as 'Crosswhite 1' in some of his publication materials. With fast-paced action and a great narrative, Dugoni's return shall be greeted with much applause by fans and newbies alike.<br /><br />Kudos, Mr. Dugoni as you return with much to show for your time away from published writing.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1246466658932025554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6036409445204889231" style="display:none">A good start to the series, I liked Tracey Crosswhite more than I thought I would. She is a smart, not too over the top, investigator who unfortunately must return to her home town to investigate her sisters 20 year old unsolved disappearance. Tracey and her sister were inseparable and two of the best young shooters in Washington State. When her sisters bones are found and the accused is days away from execution, Tracey starts her own investigation from scratch. One of her sisters best friends, who is now an attorney, helps Tracey and their budding romance is just enough to round out this good crime mystery. </span>

<div id="review_1144731561" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1144731561" />
    <a title="Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28831526-jean"><img alt="Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579801852p2/28831526.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1144731561?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jean" href="/user/show/28831526-jean">Jean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1144731561" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4631168765274657453">My Sister’s Grave is one of those books that had been on my “Want to Read” list for a while. Now that I’ve read it, I am still trying to figure out how to rate it. Did I like it? Yes. Did I love it? Not quite. I’m hoping that in the process of reviewing the novel, I will be able to decide for myself how much I liked it.<br/><br/>I was first introduced to Robert Dugoni and to his main character, Tracy Crosswhite, in his short story, The Academy. Tracy, a former high school chemistry teacher and also a cham</span>
  <span id="freeText4631168765274657453" style="display:none">My Sister’s Grave is one of those books that had been on my “Want to Read” list for a while. Now that I’ve read it, I am still trying to figure out how to rate it. Did I like it? Yes. Did I love it? Not quite. I’m hoping that in the process of reviewing the novel, I will be able to decide for myself how much I liked it.<br /><br />I was first introduced to Robert Dugoni and to his main character, Tracy Crosswhite, in his short story, The Academy. Tracy, a former high school chemistry teacher and also a champion shooter, became a police officer who rose to the level of homicide detective in Seattle. Her motivation, besides solving crimes, was to determine what happened to her younger sister Sarah twenty years earlier.<br /><br />In the book’s opening chapter, human remains were discovered near her hometown in a remote area of the Cascade Mountains in Washington State. Tracy rushed to the scene and identified some of the effects found with the remains as those of her sister. She was out of her jurisdiction, and long-time Sheriff Roy Calloway did not want her poking around in his case. Still, Tracy was determined to find out what happened to her sister. She had doubts about the convicted man’s confession and the evidence that convicted him. <br /><br />There is so much to appreciate about this book. It is a blend of police procedural and legal thriller. The plot takes the reader between the childhood memories through the investigation of Sarah’s disappearance and subsequent trial of her accused murderer, alternating with Tracy’s present-day legwork to uncover the truth. The mood swings from light humor to irritation to romance to tension to fear. Throw in a raging snowstorm and some torture to really add some terror, and we get some nail-biting suspense. The characters are well developed, particularly Tracy. Perhaps she has a future with her childhood friend, lawyer Dan O’Leary, in the sequel? There were some good twists, although they weren’t a total surprise.<br /><br />I think what niggled at me a bit was that Tracy, a trained police officer, allowed herself to get into trouble. I can’t say more without giving away some significant events, but she often went solo and took chances knowing that it was dangerous to do so. One could argue that at times she had no choice, but … I will say that I loved the way she got herself out of one giant pickle of a situation! That was smart!<br /><br />Most of all, I loved the commitment and devotion Tracy had to her sister Sarah. After twenty years, she felt still responsible – and guilty – and needed to find answers so that she could finally move forward with her life. <br /><br />As expected, in the process of putting words on the screen, I have sorted out my thoughts. I give My Sister’s Grave a solid 4-Star rating.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4631168765274657453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
